The Virtue of 'Uthman: Refuting Criticisms through Prophetic Testimony
Defense of 'Uthman's actions through virtue and prophetic testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how traditional Sunni scholars defend Caliph 'Uthman's actions—especially concerning Abu Dharr—by invoking his unparalleled virtues and prophetic commendations.

Core Idea
'Uthman's actions must be interpreted favorably given his immense virtues and prophetic praises.

This lesson presents a classical defense of Caliph 'Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) against criticisms surrounding his treatment of Abu Dharr and other accusations. The author, Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi, argues that even without specific narrations, 'Uthman's manifest virtues require interpreting his actions in the best possible light.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice the flow from the Abu Dharr story to the list of virtues and finally to the refutations.
The passage is a continuous argument; trace how the author builds his case.
2
Identify the main accusations
Find the specific criticisms against 'Uthman mentioned in the passage (treatment of Abu Dharr, favoring family, abandonment). Note how the author responds to each.
The author addresses at least three distinct accusations.
3
Examine the use of prophetic hadith
List the hadiths cited about 'Uthman's virtues. Understand how they serve as evidence that his actions cannot be interpreted negatively.
These hadiths include 'my brother and companion in paradise,' shyness of angels, etc.
4
Reflect on the principle of good assumption
The author argues that even without specific narrations, 'Uthman's virtues oblige a favorable interpretation. Consider why this principle is important in Islamic theology.
This reflects the Sunni methodology of defending the Companions.
5
Summarize the defense strategies
Write a brief summary of the three main strategies: narrational justification, virtue-based interpretation, and refutation of specific accusations.
This will help consolidate the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تبصرة الأدلة لأبي المعين النسفي ج ۲ عيش الأغنياء، وكان أبو ذر يطلب منه أن يقتدي بأبي بكر وعمر - رضي الله عنهما - في رفض الزينة ومجانبة الشبهات (۱) وكان يخاشنه في الكلام في ذلك المعنى على وجه كان يذهب بهيبة الخلافة، فرأى المصلحة في أن بعثه إلى الربذة، ولا عيب في هذا ، وروي أن معاوية كتب إلى عثمان يشكو أبا ذر فكتب عثمان إلى أبي ذر يستقدمه إلى المدينة، فأبى أبو ذر ، وقال : سمعت رسول الله عليه السلام يقول: "إذا بلغت عمارة المدينة إلى موضع كذا فاخرج عنها (۲) وقد بلغت العمارة ذلك الموضع فخيره عثمان أي البلاد أحب إليه ؟ فاختار الربذة، فقال له: فاخرج إليها، ولو لم يرو شيء من هذه الوجوه لكان الواجب حمل أمر عثمان مع زهده وورعه وجلال قدره في الدين في كونه من الذين هاجروا هجرتين، وختنا لرسول الله على الابنتين وإنفاقه في نصرة الدين وتجهيز جيش المسلمين كل نفيس وخطير من الأموال ومضنون به من النعم، وكونه من المبشرين بالجنة، وقول النبي عليه السلام فيه عثمان" أخي ورفيقي في الجنة (٤) وقوله عليه السلام - لما ستر ركبته عند مجيء عثمان -: "ألا أستحي ممن تستحي منه ملائكة السماء (٥)، وقوله عليه السلام فيه وفي علي رضي الله عنهما لما أتياه في شيء: "هكذا تدخلان الجنة لا يحبكما إلا مؤمن ولا يبغضكما إلا منافق() وروي أنه عليه السلام قال في عثمان تدخل الجنة بغير حساب (۱) وحكمه له بأنه يقتل شهيدًا، وأمره له بأن لا يخلع ثوبا كساه الله إياه. في أخبار كثيرة يطول ذكرها ، ومع قول النبي عليه السلام: "الخلافة بعدي ثلاثون سنة (۲) لكان الواجب حمل أمره على وجه يليق بشأنه وجلال قدره، فكيف يجوز مع وجود هذه المعاني والأخبار حمل أمره على أقبح الوجوه وأفسدها؟!! وقد روي في تأويل ما فعل هذه الوجوه الصحيحة التي توجب دفع الطعن عنه. وما يزعمون أنه كان يؤثر أهله ويعطيهم أموالاً، جمة، فذلك محمول على أنه كان يعطيهم من ماله إذ هو الله كان ذا مال كثير، ولهذا لم يرو النكير عليه من الصحابة، ولو كان يعطي من مال المسلمين لأنكروا ذلك عليه. وما يذكرون أن أصحاب رسول الله عليه السلام قعدوا عنه وخذلوه حتى قتل وترك ثلاثا لا يدفن، ثم لم يتبعه ولم يتول أمره إلا من لا يؤبه به. فيقال: إن عثمان الله كان يمتنع عن قتالهم شفقة منه على الخلق وتوقيًا عن إراقة دماء المسلمين وكراهية أن يقال: إن قوماً جاءوا متظلمين من عامل له فأساء إليهم وقصد سفك دمائهم، وكان المهاجرون والأنصار يعرضون أنفسهم عليه
Tabsirat al-Adilla by Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi, vol. 2. [He criticized] the life of the rich, and Abu Dharr was asking him to follow Abu Bakr and Umar - may Allah be pleased with them - in rejecting adornment and avoiding ambiguous matters. And he spoke harshly to him in that matter in a way that diminished the awe of the caliphate, so he saw the benefit in sending him to al-Rabadha, and there is no fault in this. And it is narrated that Mu'awiya wrote to 'Uthman complaining about Abu Dharr, so 'Uthman wrote to Abu Dharr summoning him to Medina, but Abu Dharr refused and said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'When the building of Medina reaches such-and-such a place, then leave it' and the building had reached that place, so 'Uthman gave him a choice of which land he liked best. He chose al-Rabadha, so he said to him: 'Then go out to it.' And even if none of these reports were narrated, it would be obligatory to interpret 'Uthman's action, given his asceticism, piety, and great standing in religion – that he was among those who migrated twice, the father-in-law of the Messenger of Allah through his two daughters, his spending in supporting the religion and equipping the Muslim army with every precious and valuable wealth and coveted blessings, his being among those given glad tidings of Paradise, and the Prophet's (peace be upon him) statement about 'Uthman: 'My brother and my companion in Paradise,' and his statement (peace be upon him) – when he covered his knee at the coming of 'Uthman –: 'Should I not feel shy of one whom the angels of heaven feel shy of?' and his statement (peace be upon him) about him and 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with them both) when they came to him concerning something: 'Thus you two will enter Paradise; no one loves you but a believer and no one hates you but a hypocrite.' And it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) said concerning 'Uthman: 'You will enter Paradise without reckoning,' and his judgment that he would be killed as a martyr, and his command to him not to remove a garment that Allah had clothed him with. [There are] many reports whose mention would be lengthy. And with the Prophet's (peace be upon him) statement: 'The caliphate after me is thirty years,' it would be obligatory to interpret his matter in a way befitting his standing and great rank. So how is it permissible, given the existence of these meanings and reports, to interpret his matter in the ugliest and most corrupt ways?!! And there have been narrated in interpretation of what he did these sound ways which necessitate repelling criticism of him. And what they claim – that he favored his family and gave them abundant wealth – that is interpreted as his giving them from his own wealth, since he himself possessed much wealth, and for this reason no disapproval from the Companions was narrated; had he been giving from the wealth of the Muslims, they would have disapproved of that. And what they mention – that the Companions of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) abandoned him and let him down until he was killed and left for three days unburied, then no one followed him or took charge of his affair except those of no account – it is said: 'Uthman refrained from fighting them out of compassion for creation, avoiding the shedding of Muslim blood, and disliking that it be said that a people came complaining of a governor of his, so he treated them badly and intended to shed their blood. And the Emigrants and the Helpers were offering themselves to him.
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage is a defense of Caliph 'Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) against criticisms, specifically regarding his treatment of Abu Dharr and other accusations. The author, Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi, begins by recounting the story of Abu Dharr: Abu Dharr criticized the lifestyle of the rich and urged 'Uthman to emulate the austerity of Abu Bakr and 'Umar. His harsh words undermined the dignity of the caliphate, so 'Uthman, seeing the public interest, sent him to al-Rabadha – an action the author deems blameless. He then cites an alternative narration where 'Uthman summoned Abu Dharr from Syria, but Abu Dharr refused, citing a prophetic command to leave Medina when its buildings reached a certain point. 'Uthman then let him choose a place, and he chose al-Rabadha. The author argues that even if these specific narrations were absent, one must interpret 'Uthman's actions favorably given his manifest virtues: his double migration, his marriage to two of the Prophet's daughters, his immense spending for Islam, his being given glad tidings of Paradise, and numerous prophetic praises (e.g., 'My brother and my companion in Paradise,' 'Shy of him whom the angels are shy of,' 'Only a believer loves you two,' 'You will enter Paradise without reckoning,' his martyrdom, and the command not to remove the garment Allah gave him). With such merits, it is impossible to interpret 'Uthman's actions in the worst possible light. The author then addresses two specific accusations: First, that 'Uthman favored his family with wealth. The author responds that he gave from his own wealth, not from the public treasury; otherwise the Companions would have objected, but no such objection is recorded. Second, that the Companions abandoned him and he was left unburied for three days. The author explains that 'Uthman refrained from fighting rebels out of mercy and fear of Muslim bloodshed, and that the Emigrants and Helpers actually offered themselves to defend him.

أبو ذر
الربذة
المبشرون بالجنة
المهاجرون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sending Abu Dharr to al-Rabadha was a punishment or exile due to personal animosity.
Correction: The author shows it was a decision for public interest to preserve the dignity of the caliphate, and Abu Dharr himself chose that location based on a prophetic command.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why did 'Uthman send Abu Dharr to al-Rabadha?
A) Because Abu Dharr insulted him personally.
B) Because Abu Dharr's harsh words undermined the awe of the caliphate, so he saw it as beneficial for him to leave.
C) Because Mu'awiya forced him to exile Abu Dharr.
D) Because Abu Dharr refused to follow the Prophet's command.

Key Takeaway
The defense of 'Uthman relies on interpreting his actions favorably due to his high status and prophetic commendations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear negative reports about a person of known piety, do you instinctively believe them or actively seek favorable interpretations? What does your reaction reveal about your own heart? Can you commit to adopting the author's method of husn al-zann starting today?
?
The author argues that 'Uthman's virtues obligate us to interpret his actions positively. Is there someone in your life—a parent, teacher, or scholar—whose spiritual rank you have failed to honor, leading you to judge them harshly? How can you rectify that by recalling their virtues?
?
This lesson shows that even the Companions were subject to false accusations. Have you ever spread or entertained criticism of a righteous person without verifying the facts, based on their apparent actions? What change will you make to safeguard your tongue and heart from similar injustice?

The Esteemed Status of Uthman and Favorable Interpretation
Establishes Uthman's high status and principle of favorable interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how prophetic reports establish Uthman's high rank and why his actions must be interpreted positively.

Core Idea
Uthman's virtues necessitate interpreting his actions in the best possible light.

This passage begins by reminding us of the lofty status of Uthman ibn Affan, citing reports that he will enter Paradise without account, die a martyr, and was commanded not to remove the garment of caliphate. These reports, along with the hadith about the thirty-year caliphate, form the basis for interpreting Uthman's actions in the most favorable manner possible.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text about Uthman's virtues and the principle of interpretation. Let the author's emphasis on prophetic reports sink in.
Note the specific reports: entry to Paradise, martyrdom, garment.
2
Identify the key reports
Identify the three reports mentioned: entering Paradise without account, being killed as a martyr, and the command not to remove the garment. Also note the hadith of 30-year caliphate.
3
Grasp the interpretive principle
Understand that given these virtues, any interpretation of Uthman's actions must be favorable, not in the ugliest manner.
This principle underpins the refutations that follow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في عثمان تدخل الجنة بغير حساب وحكمه له بأنه يقتل شهيدًا، وأمره له بأن لا يخلع ثوبا كساه الله إياه. في أخبار كثيرة يطول ذكرها، ومع قول النبي عليه السلام: "الخلافة بعدي ثلاثون سنة" لكان الواجب حمل أمره على وجه يليق بشأنه وجلال قدره، فكيف يجوز مع وجود هذه المعاني والأخبار حمل أمره على أقبح الوجوه وأفسدها؟!! وقد روي في تأويل ما فعل هذه الوجوه الصحيحة التي توجب دفع الطعن عنه. وما يزعمون أنه كان يؤثر أهله ويعطيهم أموالاً جمة، فذلك محمول على أنه كان يعطيهم من ماله إذ هو الله كان ذا مال كثير، ولهذا لم يرو النكير عليه من الصحابة، ولو كان يعطي من مال المسلمين لأنكروا ذلك عليه.
وما يذكرون أن أصحاب رسول الله عليه السلام قعدوا عنه وخذلوه حتى قتل وترك ثلاثا لا يدفن، ثم لم يتبعه ولم يتول أمره إلا من لا يؤبه به.
فيقال: إن عثمان الله كان يمتنع عن قتالهم شفقة منه على الخلق وتوقيًا عن إراقة دماء المسلمين وكراهية أن يقال: إن قوماً جاءوا متظلمين من عامل له فأساء إليهم وقصد سفك دمائهم، وكان المهاجرون والأنصار يعرضون أنفسهم عليه ويسألون منه أن يأذن لهم في محاربتهم، فكان يمتنع عن ذلك لما مر من المعاني ذلك كان الحسن والحسين وقنبر - رضي الله عنهم - حضروا الدار ودفعوا حتى خرجوا وعقروا ولم يكن عنده ولا عند أحد من الصحابة – رضي الله عنهم - أن الأمر يبلغ ذلك المبلغ ولكن نفذ فيه قضاء الله المحتوم ونالته الشهادة التي كتبت له.
وما قالوا: أنه انه ترك ثلاثاً فإنه لا يصح ذلك البتة، وكيف يظن بالمهاجرين والأنصار - رضي الله عنهم - وخصوصا بعلي الا الله ولو مات بجوارهم يهودي أو نصراني ما كانوا يرضون بأن يتركوه حرز السباع لا يوارون سوأته ولا يسترون عورته، فكيف جوزوا ذلك في عثمان مع سابقته في الإسلام وآثاره في الدين واتصاله برسول الله بابنتيه وبشارة النبي عليه السلام إياه بالجنة، فهذا والله هو الطعن الظاهر على الصحابة عموماً وعلى على الله خصوصا، ولو ثبت ذلك لكان الطعن بذلك عائدًا على من استجاز ذلك في مثله لا إليه إلا أن يكونوا تشاغلوا بعقد الإمامة وتسكين الفتنة خوفًا على الناس أن يتشتتوا وتتفرق كلمتهم، فيوجب حدوث ذلك وهنا في الإسلام، ثم تفرغوا بعد ذلك لأمره وأخذوا في تجهيزه ودفنه رضوان الله عليه.
وما يروون أنه كتب يوم الحصار إلى علي: فإن كنتُ مأكولاً فكن خير آكل وإلا فأدركني ولما أمزق - فلا أصل له إذ المعروف من أمر عثمان الله أنه كان يتحامى من الحرب ويتجوز عن ذلك حتى قال: من وضع السلاح من غلماني فهو حر. ومن كان هذا مع من قصد الحرب من غلمانه فعله فكيف
Regarding Uthman: he enters Paradise without account, and the ruling that he is killed as a martyr, and the command that he not remove a garment that God clothed him with. There are many reports that would be lengthy to mention. And with the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'The caliphate after me is thirty years,' it would be obligatory to interpret his affair in a manner befitting his status and grandeur. How is it permissible, given the existence of these meanings and reports, to interpret his affair in the ugliest and most corrupt ways?!! And it has been reported in the interpretation of what he did these correct interpretations that necessitate repelling criticism against him. And what they claim that he favored his family and gave them abundant wealth, that is interpreted as that he gave them from his own wealth, since he was a man of great wealth. For this reason, disapproval from the Companions is not reported, and if he had given from the wealth of the Muslims, they would have disapproved of that. And what they mention that the Companions of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, sat back from him and abandoned him until he was killed and left for three days unburied, then no one followed him or took charge of his affair except those who are not regarded. It is said: Uthman refrained from fighting them out of compassion for creation and caution against shedding the blood of Muslims, and dislike that it be said that a people came complaining of an agent of his who wronged them and intended to shed their blood. The Emigrants and Helpers offered themselves to him and asked him to permit them to fight them, but he refrained from that due to the meanings mentioned. That was when al-Hasan, al-Husayn, and Qanbar – may God be pleased with them – attended the house and defended until they came out and were wounded. It was not with him or any of the Companions that the matter would reach that extent, but the decree of God prevailed and he attained the martyrdom that was written for him. And what they said that he was left for three days is not true at all. How can it be thought of the Emigrants and Helpers – may God be pleased with them – especially Ali, and if a Jew or Christian had died beside them, they would not have been content to leave him as prey to beasts without covering his private parts or concealing his nakedness. So how could they permit that regarding Uthman, with his precedence in Islam, his effects in the religion, his connection to the Messenger of God through his two daughters, and the Prophet's glad tidings to him of Paradise? This, by God, is a clear criticism of the Companions in general and of Ali in particular. If that were established, the criticism would return upon whoever deemed that permissible regarding the likes of him, not upon him, unless they were occupied with establishing the imamate and calming the sedition, fearing that the people would disperse and their word become divided, causing weakness in Islam. Then after that they attended to his affair and began preparing and burying him, may God be pleased with him. And what they narrate that he wrote on the day of the siege to Ali: 'If I am to be eaten, then be the best eater; otherwise, save me and do not tear [me]' – it has no basis. For what is known of Uthman's affair is that he avoided war and excused himself from that until he said: 'Whoever of my servants lays down his weapon is free.' And this being his action with those of his servants who intended war, how [could he write such a thing]?
Source pages p. 504

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of various accusations against the third caliph, Uthman ibn Affan (رضي الله عنه). The author begins by establishing the high status of Uthman through prophetic reports: he enters Paradise without account, is a martyr, and is commanded not to remove a garment God gave him. With the hadith that the caliphate lasts thirty years, Uthman's actions must be interpreted favorably. The first accusation is that Uthman gave abundant wealth to his relatives. The author explains that he gave from his own wealth, not from public funds; otherwise the Companions would have objected. Second, the claim that the Companions abandoned Uthman until he was killed and left unburied for three days is refuted by stating that Uthman himself prevented them from fighting out of mercy and to avoid Muslim bloodshed. Al-Hasan, al-Husayn, and Qanbar actually defended him. The third accusation about delayed burial is refuted as impossible given the character of the Companions, especially Ali, who would not even leave a Jew or Christian unburied. The delay is excused by their preoccupation with appointing the next caliph and calming the fitna. Finally, the fabricated letter to Ali is rejected as baseless, given Uthman's known aversion to war, to the extent that he freed any servant who laid down arms.

Checkpoint
What is the main principle established in this passage?
A) Uthman was a martyr.
B) Uthman's actions must be interpreted in the best possible light due to his virtues.
C) The caliphate lasted exactly 30 years.
D) Uthman gave away his wealth.

Key Takeaway
Uthman's prophetic accolades demand that any criticism of his actions be interpreted in the best possible manner.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear criticism of Uthman, do you instinctively assume the worst, or do you defend him? What does that say about your heart towards the Companions?
?
The Prophet commanded Uthman not to remove a garment God clothed him with. Is there a 'garment' of responsibility that God has placed on you that you are tempted to remove? What would it mean for you to trust God's wisdom in keeping it on?
?
The author says it is 'obligatory' to interpret Uthman's affair in a manner befitting his status. Are you willing to extend that same obligation to Muslims today who have known virtue? Who in your life do you need to reinterpret favorably?

Refuting the Wealth Accusation Against Uthman
Refutes accusation that Uthman gave public wealth to relatives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the claim that Uthman misused public funds to favor his relatives.

Core Idea
Uthman gave his own wealth, not Muslim funds; companions would have objected otherwise.

A common accusation against Uthman is that he favored his family by giving them large sums from the public treasury. This lesson presents the author's clear refutation: Uthman was personally wealthy and gave from his own money, and the lack of complaint from other Companions proves it was not from Muslim funds.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage on wealth
Read the short Arabic passage where the author addresses the wealth accusation. Note the logical structure: claim, then refutation.
2
Identify the refutation's logic
The author says Uthman gave from his own wealth. Identify the two supporting points: Uthman's personal wealth and lack of objection from Companions.
3
Consider the implication
Reflect on why the silence of the Companions is significant—if it were public money, they would have criticized him.
This shows the Companions' integrity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في عثمان تدخل الجنة بغير حساب وحكمه له بأنه يقتل شهيدًا، وأمره له بأن لا يخلع ثوبا كساه الله إياه. في أخبار كثيرة يطول ذكرها، ومع قول النبي عليه السلام: "الخلافة بعدي ثلاثون سنة" لكان الواجب حمل أمره على وجه يليق بشأنه وجلال قدره، فكيف يجوز مع وجود هذه المعاني والأخبار حمل أمره على أقبح الوجوه وأفسدها؟!! وقد روي في تأويل ما فعل هذه الوجوه الصحيحة التي توجب دفع الطعن عنه. وما يزعمون أنه كان يؤثر أهله ويعطيهم أموالاً جمة، فذلك محمول على أنه كان يعطيهم من ماله إذ هو الله كان ذا مال كثير، ولهذا لم يرو النكير عليه من الصحابة، ولو كان يعطي من مال المسلمين لأنكروا ذلك عليه.
وما يذكرون أن أصحاب رسول الله عليه السلام قعدوا عنه وخذلوه حتى قتل وترك ثلاثا لا يدفن، ثم لم يتبعه ولم يتول أمره إلا من لا يؤبه به.
فيقال: إن عثمان الله كان يمتنع عن قتالهم شفقة منه على الخلق وتوقيًا عن إراقة دماء المسلمين وكراهية أن يقال: إن قوماً جاءوا متظلمين من عامل له فأساء إليهم وقصد سفك دمائهم، وكان المهاجرون والأنصار يعرضون أنفسهم عليه ويسألون منه أن يأذن لهم في محاربتهم، فكان يمتنع عن ذلك لما مر من المعاني ذلك كان الحسن والحسين وقنبر - رضي الله عنهم - حضروا الدار ودفعوا حتى خرجوا وعقروا ولم يكن عنده ولا عند أحد من الصحابة – رضي الله عنهم - أن الأمر يبلغ ذلك المبلغ ولكن نفذ فيه قضاء الله المحتوم ونالته الشهادة التي كتبت له.
وما قالوا: أنه انه ترك ثلاثاً فإنه لا يصح ذلك البتة، وكيف يظن بالمهاجرين والأنصار - رضي الله عنهم - وخصوصا بعلي الا الله ولو مات بجوارهم يهودي أو نصراني ما كانوا يرضون بأن يتركوه حرز السباع لا يوارون سوأته ولا يسترون عورته، فكيف جوزوا ذلك في عثمان مع سابقته في الإسلام وآثاره في الدين واتصاله برسول الله بابنتيه وبشارة النبي عليه السلام إياه بالجنة، فهذا والله هو الطعن الظاهر على الصحابة عموماً وعلى على الله خصوصا، ولو ثبت ذلك لكان الطعن بذلك عائدًا على من استجاز ذلك في مثله لا إليه إلا أن يكونوا تشاغلوا بعقد الإمامة وتسكين الفتنة خوفًا على الناس أن يتشتتوا وتتفرق كلمتهم، فيوجب حدوث ذلك وهنا في الإسلام، ثم تفرغوا بعد ذلك لأمره وأخذوا في تجهيزه ودفنه رضوان الله عليه.
وما يروون أنه كتب يوم الحصار إلى علي: فإن كنتُ مأكولاً فكن خير آكل وإلا فأدركني ولما أمزق - فلا أصل له إذ المعروف من أمر عثمان الله أنه كان يتحامى من الحرب ويتجوز عن ذلك حتى قال: من وضع السلاح من غلماني فهو حر. ومن كان هذا مع من قصد الحرب من غلمانه فعله فكيف
Regarding Uthman: he enters Paradise without account, and the ruling that he is killed as a martyr, and the command that he not remove a garment that God clothed him with. There are many reports that would be lengthy to mention. And with the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'The caliphate after me is thirty years,' it would be obligatory to interpret his affair in a manner befitting his status and grandeur. How is it permissible, given the existence of these meanings and reports, to interpret his affair in the ugliest and most corrupt ways?!! And it has been reported in the interpretation of what he did these correct interpretations that necessitate repelling criticism against him. And what they claim that he favored his family and gave them abundant wealth, that is interpreted as that he gave them from his own wealth, since he was a man of great wealth. For this reason, disapproval from the Companions is not reported, and if he had given from the wealth of the Muslims, they would have disapproved of that. And what they mention that the Companions of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, sat back from him and abandoned him until he was killed and left for three days unburied, then no one followed him or took charge of his affair except those who are not regarded. It is said: Uthman refrained from fighting them out of compassion for creation and caution against shedding the blood of Muslims, and dislike that it be said that a people came complaining of an agent of his who wronged them and intended to shed their blood. The Emigrants and Helpers offered themselves to him and asked him to permit them to fight them, but he refrained from that due to the meanings mentioned. That was when al-Hasan, al-Husayn, and Qanbar – may God be pleased with them – attended the house and defended until they came out and were wounded. It was not with him or any of the Companions that the matter would reach that extent, but the decree of God prevailed and he attained the martyrdom that was written for him. And what they said that he was left for three days is not true at all. How can it be thought of the Emigrants and Helpers – may God be pleased with them – especially Ali, and if a Jew or Christian had died beside them, they would not have been content to leave him as prey to beasts without covering his private parts or concealing his nakedness. So how could they permit that regarding Uthman, with his precedence in Islam, his effects in the religion, his connection to the Messenger of God through his two daughters, and the Prophet's glad tidings to him of Paradise? This, by God, is a clear criticism of the Companions in general and of Ali in particular. If that were established, the criticism would return upon whoever deemed that permissible regarding the likes of him, not upon him, unless they were occupied with establishing the imamate and calming the sedition, fearing that the people would disperse and their word become divided, causing weakness in Islam. Then after that they attended to his affair and began preparing and burying him, may God be pleased with him. And what they narrate that he wrote on the day of the siege to Ali: 'If I am to be eaten, then be the best eater; otherwise, save me and do not tear [me]' – it has no basis. For what is known of Uthman's affair is that he avoided war and excused himself from that until he said: 'Whoever of my servants lays down his weapon is free.' And this being his action with those of his servants who intended war, how [could he write such a thing]?
Source pages p. 504

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of various accusations against the third caliph, Uthman ibn Affan (رضي الله عنه). The author begins by establishing the high status of Uthman through prophetic reports: he enters Paradise without account, is a martyr, and is commanded not to remove a garment God gave him. With the hadith that the caliphate lasts thirty years, Uthman's actions must be interpreted favorably. The first accusation is that Uthman gave abundant wealth to his relatives. The author explains that he gave from his own wealth, not from public funds; otherwise the Companions would have objected. Second, the claim that the Companions abandoned Uthman until he was killed and left unburied for three days is refuted by stating that Uthman himself prevented them from fighting out of mercy and to avoid Muslim bloodshed. Al-Hasan, al-Husayn, and Qanbar actually defended him. The third accusation about delayed burial is refuted as impossible given the character of the Companions, especially Ali, who would not even leave a Jew or Christian unburied. The delay is excused by their preoccupation with appointing the next caliph and calming the fitna. Finally, the fabricated letter to Ali is rejected as baseless, given Uthman's known aversion to war, to the extent that he freed any servant who laid down arms.

Key Terms
عثمان
الصحابة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that Uthman did not give from Muslim funds?
A) Because Uthman was poor and had no money.
B) Because the Companions did not criticize him, and if he had used public money they would have.
C) Because the accusation is fabricated.
D) Because Uthman's relatives were poor.

Key Takeaway
Uthman gave from his own wealth, and the Companions' silence confirms no public misuse occurred.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are accused of something wrong, do you immediately defend yourself with evidence, or do you rely on your reputation? Uthman's defense was based on objective proof. Think of a recent accusation you faced. Did you respond like him? Commit to gathering factual evidence next time instead of just denying.
?
Whose silence in your life would worry you if they said nothing about your actions? If those who know you best remained silent, would it be because they approve or because they are afraid of you? The Companions' silence was proof of Uthman's correctness. Examine one relationship where silence may not mean agreement. Seek honest feedback this week.
?
Uthman gave generously from his own wealth to his family. Do you give from what is truly yours, or do you fund your generosity with what belongs to others (e.g., time or resources owed elsewhere)? Look at your giving in the past month. Make a specific plan to give something personal—time, money, or skill—to a family member today.

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
6 min
Uthman's Abandonment and Burial Refuted
Refutes claims of abandonment, lack of defense, and delayed burial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's refutation of claims that the Companions abandoned Uthman and left him unburied for three days.

Core Idea
Uthman prevented fighting, Companions offered support, and delayed burial was due to caliphate transition.

Among the most serious allegations are that the Companions failed to defend Uthman during the siege and left his body unburied for three days. The author responds by explaining Uthman's own refusal to fight, the presence of defenders like al-Hasan and al-Husayn, and the impossibility that the Companions would neglect a burial, especially that of such a high-ranking figure. Any delay was due to the pressing need to establish the next caliph and calm the fitna.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on abandonment and burial
Read the Arabic text carefully. It covers multiple sub-claims: that Companions sat back, that Uthman was left unburied, and that only unworthy people attended to him.
2
Identify the three refutations
The author refutes each claim: (1) Uthman himself refused to fight to avoid bloodshed, (2) al-Hasan and al-Husayn defended him, (3) the burial delay is false and explained by preoccupation with caliphate.
Also note the defense of Ali.
3
Reflect on the argument's strength
Consider how the author uses the character of the Companions, especially Ali, to argue that they would never leave anyone unburied.
This is a powerful rhetorical point.

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of various accusations against the third caliph, Uthman ibn Affan (رضي الله عنه). The author begins by establishing the high status of Uthman through prophetic reports: he enters Paradise without account, is a martyr, and is commanded not to remove a garment God gave him. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author's defense of Uthman implies criticism of the Companions who failed him.
Correction: The author argues that the Companions did not abandon him; rather, Uthman himself prevented fighting, and the Companions were later occupied with establishing the caliphate.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why was Uthman's burial possibly delayed?
A) The Companions did not care about him.
B) Uthman's body was not found.
C) The Companions were occupied with establishing the caliphate and calming the fitna.
D) There was no delay; he was buried immediately.

Key Takeaway
Uthman prevented defense to avoid bloodshed, and the Companions' character precludes neglect; any burial delay was for pressing political reasons.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a fellow believer suffering, do you offer help even if they refuse? The Companions offered themselves despite Uthman's refusal. What stops you from repeatedly offering support to those in need?
?
If you were in Ali's position, would you prioritize the immediate burial of a martyr or the long-term stability of the Muslim community? What does your answer reveal about your sense of responsibility?
?
The author says that not even a Jew or Christian would be left unburied by the Companions. How does this standard challenge your own care for the dignity of others, especially those you disagree with?

The Fabricated Letter to Ali Refuted
Rejects fabricated letter as baseless due to Uthman's known character.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author rejects the story that Uthman wrote a desperate poem to Ali during the siege as baseless.

Core Idea
The letter is fabricated because it contradicts Uthman's known aversion to war.

Some narrations claim that during the siege, Uthman wrote a line of poetry to Ali asking him to either be the eater or save him from being torn. The author dismisses this as having no foundation, pointing out that Uthman was known to abhor war so much that he freed any servant who laid down his arms. This character trait makes the poem impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage about the letter
Read the short passage where the author mentions the alleged letter and its refutation.
The Arabic text cuts off, but the argument is clear.
2
Identify the accusation and refutation
The accusation is that Uthman wrote a poetic line to Ali. The refutation denies its authenticity and cites Uthman's known pacifism.
3
Understand the logic
Uthman's statement freeing any servant who laid down arms shows his extreme reluctance to fight, contradicting the desperate tone of the poem.
This is a simple but effective argument.

وما يذكرون أن أصحاب رسول الله عليه السلام قعدوا عنه وخذلوه حتى قتل وترك ثلاثا لا يدفن، ثم لم يتبعه ولم يتول أمره إلا من لا يؤبه به.
فيقال: إن عثمان الله كان يمتنع عن قتالهم شفقة منه على الخلق وتوقيًا عن إراقة دماء المسلمين وكراهية أن يقال: إن قوماً جاءوا متظلمين من عامل له فأساء إليهم وقصد سفك دمائهم، وكان المهاجرون والأنصار يعرضون أنفسهم عليه ويسألون منه أن يأذن لهم في محاربتهم، فكان يمتنع عن ذلك لما مر من المعاني ذلك كان الحسن والحسين وقنبر - رضي الله عنهم - حضروا الدار ودفعوا حتى خرجوا وعقروا ولم يكن عنده ولا عند أحد من الصحابة – رضي الله عنهم - أن الأمر يبلغ ذلك المبلغ ولكن نفذ فيه قضاء الله المحتوم ونالته الشهادة التي كتبت له.
وما قالوا: أنه انه ترك ثلاثاً فإنه لا يصح ذلك البتة، وكيف يظن بالمهاجرين والأنصار - رضي الله عنهم - وخصوصا بعلي الا الله ولو مات بجوارهم يهودي أو نصراني ما كانوا يرضون بأن يتركوه حرز السباع لا يوارون سوأته ولا يسترون عورته، فكيف جوزوا ذلك في عثمان مع سابقته في الإسلام وآثاره في الدين واتصاله برسول الله بابنتيه وبشارة النبي عليه السلام إياه بالجنة، فهذا والله هو الطعن الظاهر على الصحابة عموماً وعلى على الله خصوصا، ولو ثبت ذلك لكان الطعن بذلك عائدًا على من استجاز ذلك في مثله لا إليه إلا أن يكونوا تشاغلوا بعقد الإمامة وتسكين الفتنة خوفًا على الناس أن يتشتتوا وتتفرق كلمتهم، فيوجب حدوث ذلك وهنا في الإسلام، ثم تفرغوا بعد ذلك لأمره وأخذوا في تجهيزه ودفنه رضوان الله عليه.
وما يروون أنه كتب يوم الحصار إلى علي: فإن كنتُ مأكولاً فكن خير آكل وإلا فأدركني ولما أمزق - فلا أصل له إذ المعروف من أمر عثمان الله أنه كان يتحامى من الحرب ويتجوز عن ذلك حتى قال: من وضع السلاح من غلماني فهو حر. ومن كان هذا مع من قصد الحرب من غلمانه فعله فكيف
Regarding Uthman: he enters Paradise without account, and the ruling that he is killed as a martyr, and the command that he not remove a garment that God clothed him with. There are many reports that would be lengthy to mention. And with the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'The caliphate after me is thirty years,' it would be obligatory to interpret his affair in a manner befitting his status and grandeur. How is it permissible, given the existence of these meanings and reports, to interpret his affair in the ugliest and most corrupt ways?!! And it has been reported in the interpretation of what he did these correct interpretations that necessitate repelling criticism against him. And what they claim that he favored his family and gave them abundant wealth, that is interpreted as that he gave them from his own wealth, since he was a man of great wealth. For this reason, disapproval from the Companions is not reported, and if he had given from the wealth of the Muslims, they would have disapproved of that. And what they mention that the Companions of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, sat back from him and abandoned him until he was killed and left for three days unburied, then no one followed him or took charge of his affair except those who are not regarded. It is said: Uthman refrained from fighting them out of compassion for creation and caution against shedding the blood of Muslims, and dislike that it be said that a people came complaining of an agent of his who wronged them and intended to shed their blood. The Emigrants and Helpers offered themselves to him and asked him to permit them to fight them, but he refrained from that due to the meanings mentioned. That was when al-Hasan, al-Husayn, and Qanbar – may God be pleased with them – attended the house and defended until they came out and were wounded. It was not with him or any of the Companions that the matter would reach that extent, but the decree of God prevailed and he attained the martyrdom that was written for him. And what they said that he was left for three days is not true at all. How can it be thought of the Emigrants and Helpers – may God be pleased with them – especially Ali, and if a Jew or Christian had died beside them, they would not have been content to leave him as prey to beasts without covering his private parts or concealing his nakedness. So how could they permit that regarding Uthman, with his precedence in Islam, his effects in the religion, his connection to the Messenger of God through his two daughters, and the Prophet's glad tidings to him of Paradise? This, by God, is a clear criticism of the Companions in general and of Ali in particular. If that were established, the criticism would return upon whoever deemed that permissible regarding the likes of him, not upon him, unless they were occupied with establishing the imamate and calming the sedition, fearing that the people would disperse and their word become divided, causing weakness in Islam. Then after that they attended to his affair and began preparing and burying him, may God be pleased with him. And what they narrate that he wrote on the day of the siege to Ali: 'If I am to be eaten, then be the best eater; otherwise, save me and do not tear [me]' – it has no basis. For what is known of Uthman's affair is that he avoided war and excused himself from that until he said: 'Whoever of my servants lays down his weapon is free.' And this being his action with those of his servants who intended war, how [could he write such a thing]?
Source pages p. 504

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of various accusations against the third caliph, Uthman ibn Affan (رضي الله عنه). The author begins by establishing the high status of Uthman through prophetic reports: he enters Paradise without account, is a martyr, and is commanded not to remove a garment God gave him. With the hadith that the caliphate lasts thirty years, Uthman's actions must be interpreted favorably. The first accusation is that Uthman gave abundant wealth to his relatives. The author explains that he gave from his own wealth, not from public funds; otherwise the Companions would have objected. Second, the claim that the Companions abandoned Uthman until he was killed and left unburied for three days is refuted by stating that Uthman himself prevented them from fighting out of mercy and to avoid Muslim bloodshed. Al-Hasan, al-Husayn, and Qanbar actually defended him. The third accusation about delayed burial is refuted as impossible given the character of the Companions, especially Ali, who would not even leave a Jew or Christian unburied. The delay is excused by their preoccupation with appointing the next caliph and calming the fitna. Finally, the fabricated letter to Ali is rejected as baseless, given Uthman's known aversion to war, to the extent that he freed any servant who laid down arms.

Key Terms
عثمان
علي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author consider the letter to Ali baseless?
A) Because Ali never received it.
B) Because it contradicts Uthman's known avoidance of war and his freeing of servants who laid down arms.
C) Because the poem is not in classical Arabic.
D) Because Uthman did not know how to write.

Key Takeaway
The alleged letter to Ali is rejected because it conflicts with Uthman's established character of avoiding war.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial, do you respond with panic or with principles rooted in faith? Uthman could have fought but chose peace. Can you point to one situation this week where you will intentionally choose principle over expediency?
?
If a false statement about you were circulated, would your known character defend you? This lesson shows that Uthman's consistent conduct refuted the lie. What habits are you building right now that would make a false accusation against you implausible?
?
Are you quick to believe narratives that paint a leader or believer in a negative light? This lesson warns against accepting stories without checking them against known character. Who have you misjudged recently, and will you seek to correct that assumption today?

Refuting the Neglect of Uthman's Corpse
Refuting the claim that Uthman's corpse was neglected for three days.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that Uthman's body was left unburied for three days is false based on the character of the Companions, especially Ali.

Core Idea
The Companions' honor makes it inconceivable they neglected Uthman's burial.

This lesson tackles a disturbing accusation: that after Uthman's murder, his body was left unburied for three days. The author argues from the known virtue of the Companions, especially Ali, that this is impossible. He then offers a plausible explanation for any delay: they were occupied with stabilizing the caliphate and preventing civil strife.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation of the three-day claim
The author first states the claim is baseless. Then he uses a comparative argument: if a non-Muslim died near them, they would still bury him decently. So how could they neglect Uthman?
Notice the rhetorical question emphasizes the absurdity.
2
Examine the counter-explanation for delay
The author suggests that if there was any delay, it was due to the urgent need to elect a new caliph and calm the fitna (sedition) to prevent further damage to the Muslim community.
This shows understanding of historical context, not neglect.
3
Reflect on the implication for Ali
The author highlights that accusing the Companions of such neglect is an open attack on Ali and all the Muhajirun and Ansar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسألون منه أن يأذن لهم في محاربتهم، فكان يمتنع عن ذلك لما مر من المعاني ذلك كان الحسن والحسين وقنبر - رضي الله عنهم - حضروا الدار ودفعوا حتى خرجوا وعقروا ولم يكن عنده ولا عند أحد من الصحابة – رضي الله عنهم - أن الأمر يبلغ ذلك المبلغ ولكن نفذ فيه قضاء الله المحتوم ونالته الشهادة التي كتبت له.
وما قالوا: أنه انه ترك ثلاثاً فإنه لا يصح ذلك البتة، وكيف يظن بالمهاجرين والأنصار - رضي الله عنهم - وخصوصا بعلي الا الله ولو مات بجوارهم يهودي أو - نصراني ما كانوا يرضون بأن يتركوه حرز السباع لا يوارون سوأته ولا يسترون عورته، فكيف جوزوا ذلك في عثمان مع سابقته في الإسلام وآثاره في الدين واتصاله برسول الله بابنتيه وبشارة النبي عليه السلام إياه بالجنة، فهذا والله هو الطعن الظاهر على الصحابة عموماً وعلى على خصوصا، ولو ثبت ذلك لكان الطعن بذلك عائدًا على من استجاز ذلك في مثله لا إليه إلا أن يكونوا تشاغلوا بعقد الإمامة وتسكين الفتنة خوفًا على الناس أن يتشتتوا وتتفرق كلمتهم، فيوجب حدوث ذلك وهنا في الإسلام، ثم تفرغوا بعد ذلك لأمره وأخذوا في تجهيزه ودفنه رضوان الله عليه.
وما يروون أنه كتب يوم الحصار إلى علي -: فإن كنتُ مأكولاً فكن خير آكل وإلا فأدركني ولما أمزق - فلا أصل له إذ المعروف من أمر عثمان أنه كان يتحامى من الحرب ويتجوز عن ذلك حتى قال: من وضع السلاح من غلماني فهو حر. ومن كان هذا - مع من قصد الحرب من غلمانه - فعله فكيف يستعين بعلي ؟! وكيف يستنصر من هو جاد في نصره مشمر ذيله في ذلك؟! وروى عنه له أنه قال : - والله ما قتلت عثمان ولا مالات في قتله - وما روي عن علي أنه قال في أمر عثمان: الله قتله وأنا معه - معناه: وأنا مع عثمان وكانت الهاء عائدة إلى عثمان دون الله تعالى، وأخبر أنه يستشهد كما استشهد عثمان رضي الله عنهما.
يحققه أنه قال على المنبر : - قتلت يوم قتل الثور الأبيض - وهو مثل مشهور في العرب، أخبر بذلك أنه يستشهد كما استشهد هو، والله الموفق.
سبب مقتل عثمان : ثم سبب قتله معروف وهو أنه كان ولى بعض أقاربه مصر فجاء أهل مصر يشكونه إليه فعزله، وولى محمد بن أبي بكر وبعثه، ثم افتعل مروان كتابا كتبه بيده وختمه بخاتم عثمان لما أنه كان بيده من غير علم لعثمان وأرسله إليه على يد راكب جمل، وظفر به وأنكر الكتاب وقال: فعله مروان، فقال له علي: لقد صدق، فصدقه علي في ذلك وعلم أنه لا يفعل مثل هذا، وكان يعينه وينصره، ولو استغاثه لدفع القوم بالحرب، وكان خرج إلى قرية يوم قتله وأقعد على باب الدار الحسن والحسين يحتطانه، فلما رجع عاتبهما فقالا: نقب عليه ولم نعلم، ولقد ترك محمد بن أبي بكر قصد قتله والإعانة عليه لما قال له: لو كان أبوك
And they ask him to allow them to fight them, but he used to refrain from that due to the meanings that have passed. That was when al-Hasan, al-Husayn, and Qanbar – may Allah be pleased with them – attended the house and repelled until they went out and were wounded, and it was not with him nor with any of the Companions – may Allah be pleased with them – that the matter would reach that extent, but the decree of Allah, the inevitable, was executed upon him, and he attained the martyrdom that was written for him. And what they said: that he was left for three days – that is not at all correct. How could it be thought of the Muhajirun and Ansar – may Allah be pleased with them – especially 'Ali? By Allah, if a Jew or Christian died near them, they would not be satisfied to leave him as a prey for beasts, not covering his private parts nor concealing his nudity. So how could they permit that for 'Uthman, with his precedence in Islam, his effects in the religion, his connection to the Messenger of Allah through his two daughters, and the Prophet's glad tidings to him of Paradise? This, by Allah, is open disparagement of the Companions in general and of 'Ali in particular. And if that were established, the disparagement would return upon the one who deemed it permissible in the likes of him, not upon him. Unless they were occupied with organizing the caliphate and calming the sedition, fearing that the people would scatter and their word become divided, which would cause weakness in Islam. Then after that, they attended to his affair and undertook his preparation and burial – may Allah be pleased with him. And what they narrate that he wrote during the siege to 'Ali: 'If I am to be eaten, then be the best eater; otherwise, save me before I am torn apart' – has no basis. For what is known of 'Uthman's affair is that he used to avoid war and overlook such, to the point that he said: 'Whoever lays down his weapon from among my servants is free.' And one whose action was this with those of his servants who intended war – how could he seek help from 'Ali?! And how could he seek victory from one who was earnest in supporting him, ready and willing in that?! And it is narrated from him that he said: 'By Allah, I did not kill 'Uthman nor did I participate in his killing.' And what is narrated from 'Ali that he said regarding 'Uthman's affair: 'Allah killed him, and I am with him' – its meaning is: 'I am with 'Uthman,' and the pronoun refers to 'Uthman, not to Allah the Exalted. And he informed that he would be martyred as 'Uthman was martyred – may Allah be pleased with them both. He confirms it by his saying on the pulpit: 'I will be killed on the day the white bull is killed' – which is a famous proverb among the Arabs. He informed by that that he would be martyred as he was martyred. And Allah is the Grantor of success. The cause of the murder of 'Uthman: Then the cause of his murder is known, which is that he had appointed some of his relatives over Egypt, and the people of Egypt came complaining to him about him, so he dismissed him and appointed Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr and sent him. Then Marwan forged a letter, wrote it with his own hand, and sealed it with 'Uthman's seal since it was in his hand, without 'Uthman's knowledge, and sent it to him on a camel rider. And it was intercepted, and he denied the letter and said: 'Marwan did it.' 'Ali said to him: 'He has told the truth.' So 'Ali affirmed him in that and knew that he would not do such a thing. And he used to assist and support him, and if he had sought his help, he would have repelled the people with war. And he had gone out to a village on the day of his murder and had al-Hasan and al-Husayn sit at the door of the house guarding him. When he returned, he reproached them, and they said: 'He was stabbed from behind and we did not know.' And indeed, Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr refrained from intending his murder and from assisting in it when he said to him: 'If your father were...'
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and explanation. The author first addresses the claim that Uthman's body was left unburied for three days. He argues that this is impossible given the piety and honor of the Companions, especially Ali, and that if they had delayed burial, it was due to urgent matters of the caliphate. He then refutes a poem allegedly written by Uthman to Ali asking for help, showing it contradicts Uthman's peaceful stance. Next, he clarifies Ali's statement 'Allah killed him and I am with him,' explaining it means Ali was with Uthman, not with Allah. He supports this by citing Ali's prophecy of his own martyrdom. Finally, he recounts the historical cause of Uthman's murder: his appointment of a relative over Egypt, the forging of a letter by Marwan, and the role of Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr. The author emphasizes Ali's innocence and support for Uthman.

Key Terms
الصحابة
المهاجرين والأنصار
عثمان
علي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Uthman's body was neglected by Ali and the Companions due to animosity.
Correction: The author shows this is impossible given their character, and any delay was due to pressing political necessities.

Checkpoint
What argument does the author use to refute the claim that Uthman was left unburied?
A) Uthman was buried immediately after death.
B) If a non-Muslim died, they would still bury him, so how could they neglect Uthman?
C) Ali personally buried Uthman.
D) The companions were too busy fighting to bury him.

Key Takeaway
The accusation that Uthman's corpse was neglected is refuted by the known honor of the Companions and a practical explanation of delay due to political stability.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If you were in 'Ali's position during a crisis, would you prioritize a funeral or stabilizing the community? The Companions did both. This calls for a balance between religious duties and social responsibilities. Where in your life have you neglected a duty due to other pressures? How can you adjust?
?
The author calls the accusation against the Companions 'open disparagement.' Think of a time you made a harsh assumption about a fellow Muslim. How can you protect your tongue from similar slander? What practical measure will you implement this week?

Refuting the Poem and Clarifying Ali's Statement
Refuting a forged poem and clarifying Ali's statement about Uthman's death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the alleged poem from Uthman to Ali is baseless and what Ali really meant by 'Allah killed him and I am with him.'

Core Idea
Uthman's known conduct refutes the poem, and Ali's words confirm his support.

This lesson addresses two forged or misinterpreted texts: a poem supposedly written by Uthman to Ali asking for help during the siege, and a statement by Ali that has been misunderstood to imply his involvement in Uthman's death. The author demonstrates the poem's inconsistency with Uthman's character and clarifies Ali's meaning, further proving Ali's innocence and support for Uthman.

Guided Path
1
Examine the refutation of the poem
Read the author's argument: the poem contradicts Uthman's well-known peaceful disposition—he even freed slaves who took up arms. How could he ask Ali for military help?
2
Understand the clarification of Ali's statement
The author explains that Ali's words 'Allah killed him and I am with him' mean 'I am with Uthman' (the pronoun refers to Uthman, not Allah). This emphasizes Ali's loyalty, not involvement.
The author uses grammar to clarify the meaning.
3
See the supporting evidence from Ali's prophecy
Ali prophesied his own martyrdom by saying 'I will be killed on the day the white bull is killed,' a proverb meaning he would die similarly. This confirms his innocence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وما قالوا: أنه انه ترك ثلاثاً فإنه لا يصح ذلك البتة، وكيف يظن بالمهاجرين والأنصار - رضي الله عنهم - وخصوصا بعلي الا الله ولو مات بجوارهم يهودي أو - نصراني ما كانوا يرضون بأن يتركوه حرز السباع لا يوارون سوأته ولا يسترون عورته، فكيف جوزوا ذلك في عثمان مع سابقته في الإسلام وآثاره في الدين واتصاله برسول الله بابنتيه وبشارة النبي عليه السلام إياه بالجنة، فهذا والله هو الطعن الظاهر على الصحابة عموماً وعلى على خصوصا، ولو ثبت ذلك لكان الطعن بذلك عائدًا على من استجاز ذلك في مثله لا إليه إلا أن يكونوا تشاغلوا بعقد الإمامة وتسكين الفتنة خوفًا على الناس أن يتشتتوا وتتفرق كلمتهم، فيوجب حدوث ذلك وهنا في الإسلام، ثم تفرغوا بعد ذلك لأمره وأخذوا في تجهيزه ودفنه رضوان الله عليه.
وما يروون أنه كتب يوم الحصار إلى علي -: فإن كنتُ مأكولاً فكن خير آكل وإلا فأدركني ولما أمزق - فلا أصل له إذ المعروف من أمر عثمان أنه كان يتحامى من الحرب ويتجوز عن ذلك حتى قال: من وضع السلاح من غلماني فهو حر. ومن كان هذا - مع من قصد الحرب من غلمانه - فعله فكيف يستعين بعلي ؟! وكيف يستنصر من هو جاد في نصره مشمر ذيله في ذلك؟! وروى عنه له أنه قال : - والله ما قتلت عثمان ولا مالات في قتله - وما روي عن علي أنه قال في أمر عثمان: الله قتله وأنا معه - معناه: وأنا مع عثمان وكانت الهاء عائدة إلى عثمان دون الله تعالى، وأخبر أنه يستشهد كما استشهد عثمان رضي الله عنهما.
يحققه أنه قال على المنبر : - قتلت يوم قتل الثور الأبيض - وهو مثل مشهور في العرب، أخبر بذلك أنه يستشهد كما استشهد هو، والله الموفق.
سبب مقتل عثمان : ثم سبب قتله معروف وهو أنه كان ولى بعض أقاربه مصر فجاء أهل مصر يشكونه إليه فعزله، وولى محمد بن أبي بكر وبعثه، ثم افتعل مروان كتابا كتبه بيده وختمه بخاتم عثمان لما أنه كان بيده من غير علم لعثمان وأرسله إليه على يد راكب جمل، وظفر به وأنكر الكتاب وقال: فعله مروان، فقال له علي: لقد صدق، فصدقه علي في ذلك وعلم أنه لا يفعل مثل هذا، وكان يعينه وينصره، ولو استغاثه لدفع القوم بالحرب، وكان خرج إلى قرية يوم قتله وأقعد على باب الدار الحسن والحسين يحتطانه، فلما رجع عاتبهما فقالا: نقب عليه ولم نعلم، ولقد ترك محمد بن أبي بكر قصد قتله والإعانة عليه لما قال له: لو كان أبوك
And they ask him to allow them to fight them, but he used to refrain from that due to the meanings that have passed. That was when al-Hasan, al-Husayn, and Qanbar – may Allah be pleased with them – attended the house and repelled until they went out and were wounded, and it was not with him nor with any of the Companions – may Allah be pleased with them – that the matter would reach that extent, but the decree of Allah, the inevitable, was executed upon him, and he attained the martyrdom that was written for him. And what they said: that he was left for three days – that is not at all correct. How could it be thought of the Muhajirun and Ansar – may Allah be pleased with them – especially 'Ali? By Allah, if a Jew or Christian died near them, they would not be satisfied to leave him as a prey for beasts, not covering his private parts nor concealing his nudity. So how could they permit that for 'Uthman, with his precedence in Islam, his effects in the religion, his connection to the Messenger of Allah through his two daughters, and the Prophet's glad tidings to him of Paradise? This, by Allah, is open disparagement of the Companions in general and of 'Ali in particular. And if that were established, the disparagement would return upon the one who deemed it permissible in the likes of him, not upon him. Unless they were occupied with organizing the caliphate and calming the sedition, fearing that the people would scatter and their word become divided, which would cause weakness in Islam. Then after that, they attended to his affair and undertook his preparation and burial – may Allah be pleased with him. And what they narrate that he wrote during the siege to 'Ali: 'If I am to be eaten, then be the best eater; otherwise, save me before I am torn apart' – has no basis. For what is known of 'Uthman's affair is that he used to avoid war and overlook such, to the point that he said: 'Whoever lays down his weapon from among my servants is free.' And one whose action was this with those of his servants who intended war – how could he seek help from 'Ali?! And how could he seek victory from one who was earnest in supporting him, ready and willing in that?! And it is narrated from him that he said: 'By Allah, I did not kill 'Uthman nor did I participate in his killing.' And what is narrated from 'Ali that he said regarding 'Uthman's affair: 'Allah killed him, and I am with him' – its meaning is: 'I am with 'Uthman,' and the pronoun refers to 'Uthman, not to Allah the Exalted. And he informed that he would be martyred as 'Uthman was martyred – may Allah be pleased with them both. He confirms it by his saying on the pulpit: 'I will be killed on the day the white bull is killed' – which is a famous proverb among the Arabs. He informed by that that he would be martyred as he was martyred. And Allah is the Grantor of success. The cause of the murder of 'Uthman: Then the cause of his murder is known, which is that he had appointed some of his relatives over Egypt, and the people of Egypt came complaining to him about him, so he dismissed him and appointed Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr and sent him. Then Marwan forged a letter, wrote it with his own hand, and sealed it with 'Uthman's seal since it was in his hand, without 'Uthman's knowledge, and sent it to him on a camel rider. And it was intercepted, and he denied the letter and said: 'Marwan did it.' 'Ali said to him: 'He has told the truth.' So 'Ali affirmed him in that and knew that he would not do such a thing. And he used to assist and support him, and if he had sought his help, he would have repelled the people with war. And he had gone out to a village on the day of his murder and had al-Hasan and al-Husayn sit at the door of the house guarding him. When he returned, he reproached them, and they said: 'He was stabbed from behind and we did not know.' And indeed, Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr refrained from intending his murder and from assisting in it when he said to him: 'If your father were...'
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and explanation. The author first addresses the claim that Uthman's body was left unburied for three days. He argues that this is impossible given the piety and honor of the Companions, especially Ali, and that if they had delayed burial, it was due to urgent matters of the caliphate. He then refutes a poem allegedly written by Uthman to Ali asking for help, showing it contradicts Uthman's peaceful stance. Next, he clarifies Ali's statement 'Allah killed him and I am with him,' explaining it means Ali was with Uthman, not with Allah. He supports this by citing Ali's prophecy of his own martyrdom. Finally, he recounts the historical cause of Uthman's murder: his appointment of a relative over Egypt, the forging of a letter by Marwan, and the role of Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr. The author emphasizes Ali's innocence and support for Uthman.

Key Terms
عثمان
علي
مروان
الثور الأبيض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Ali said 'Allah killed him and I am with him' meaning he was with Allah in killing Uthman.
Correction: The pronoun 'him' refers to Uthman, so Ali was declaring his support for Uthman, not participation in his death.

Checkpoint
How does the author refute the poem attributed to Uthman?
A) By showing it is not found in any reliable book.
B) By showing it contradicts Uthman's peaceful character.
C) By showing it was written by Ali.
D) By showing it was written by Marwan.

Key Takeaway
The alleged poem is false, and Ali's statement actually confirms his support for Uthman, further clarified by his prophecy of his own martyrdom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a story about a companion that paints them in a negative light, do you automatically accept it or do you verify it against their established character and authentic reports? How will you change your approach after learning from this lesson?
?
If you were in Ali's position, facing false accusations about your stance on a fellow believer's death, would you have the courage to clarify and defend the truth even if it exposes you to further criticism? What step will you take today to defend the honor of a Muslim being slandered?
?
The lesson shows how a single misinterpreted pronoun can lead to a grave misunderstanding. Think of a time you jumped to a conclusion about someone's words or actions. Are you willing to go back and reassess with the same carefulness shown here? Write down one relationship you will seek to correct.

The Cause of Uthman's Murder and Ali's Innocence
Narrating the historical cause of Uthman's murder and exonerating Ali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical cause of Uthman's murder, including the role of Marwan's forged letter and Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr, and how Ali was innocent and supportive.

Core Idea
Uthman's murder was caused by a forged letter, not by Ali or the Companions.

This lesson presents the historical background of Uthman's murder as recorded by the author. The cause involves Uthman appointing a relative over Egypt, complaints from the people, and the forging of a letter by Marwan that incited the rebels. The author emphasizes that Ali did not participate and even attempted to defend Uthman, as shown by his sons being posted at the door. Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr's role is also clarified.

Guided Path
1
Understand the grievance of the Egyptians
Uthman appointed a relative (Walid ibn Uqba or others) over Egypt; the people complained, so he replaced him with Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr.
2
Identify the forgery by Marwan
Marwan forged a letter with Uthman's seal without his knowledge, ordering the punishment of the complainants. This was intercepted, leading to the siege.
Ali affirmed that Uthman was truthful about the forgery.
3
Note Ali's support and defense efforts
Ali assisted Uthman, and on the day of the murder, he had placed his sons Hasan and Husayn at the door to guard him. They did not prevent the stabbing from a hidden direction.
The author also mentions Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr refrained from killing when reminded of his father.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسألون منه أن يأذن لهم في محاربتهم، فكان يمتنع عن ذلك لما مر من المعاني ذلك كان الحسن والحسين وقنبر - رضي الله عنهم - حضروا الدار ودفعوا حتى خرجوا وعقروا ولم يكن عنده ولا عند أحد من الصحابة – رضي الله عنهم - أن الأمر يبلغ ذلك المبلغ ولكن نفذ فيه قضاء الله المحتوم ونالته الشهادة التي كتبت له.
وما قالوا: أنه انه ترك ثلاثاً فإنه لا يصح ذلك البتة، وكيف يظن بالمهاجرين والأنصار - رضي الله عنهم - وخصوصا بعلي الا الله ولو مات بجوارهم يهودي أو - نصراني ما كانوا يرضون بأن يتركوه حرز السباع لا يوارون سوأته ولا يسترون عورته، فكيف جوزوا ذلك في عثمان مع سابقته في الإسلام وآثاره في الدين واتصاله برسول الله بابنتيه وبشارة النبي عليه السلام إياه بالجنة، فهذا والله هو الطعن الظاهر على الصحابة عموماً وعلى على خصوصا، ولو ثبت ذلك لكان الطعن بذلك عائدًا على من استجاز ذلك في مثله لا إليه إلا أن يكونوا تشاغلوا بعقد الإمامة وتسكين الفتنة خوفًا على الناس أن يتشتتوا وتتفرق كلمتهم، فيوجب حدوث ذلك وهنا في الإسلام، ثم تفرغوا بعد ذلك لأمره وأخذوا في تجهيزه ودفنه رضوان الله عليه.
وما يروون أنه كتب يوم الحصار إلى علي -: فإن كنتُ مأكولاً فكن خير آكل وإلا فأدركني ولما أمزق - فلا أصل له إذ المعروف من أمر عثمان أنه كان يتحامى من الحرب ويتجوز عن ذلك حتى قال: من وضع السلاح من غلماني فهو حر. ومن كان هذا - مع من قصد الحرب من غلمانه - فعله فكيف يستعين بعلي ؟! وكيف يستنصر من هو جاد في نصره مشمر ذيله في ذلك؟! وروى عنه له أنه قال : - والله ما قتلت عثمان ولا مالات في قتله - وما روي عن علي أنه قال في أمر عثمان: الله قتله وأنا معه - معناه: وأنا مع عثمان وكانت الهاء عائدة إلى عثمان دون الله تعالى، وأخبر أنه يستشهد كما استشهد عثمان رضي الله عنهما.
يحققه أنه قال على المنبر : - قتلت يوم قتل الثور الأبيض - وهو مثل مشهور في العرب، أخبر بذلك أنه يستشهد كما استشهد هو، والله الموفق.
سبب مقتل عثمان : ثم سبب قتله معروف وهو أنه كان ولى بعض أقاربه مصر فجاء أهل مصر يشكونه إليه فعزله، وولى محمد بن أبي بكر وبعثه، ثم افتعل مروان كتابا كتبه بيده وختمه بخاتم عثمان لما أنه كان بيده من غير علم لعثمان وأرسله إليه على يد راكب جمل، وظفر به وأنكر الكتاب وقال: فعله مروان، فقال له علي: لقد صدق، فصدقه علي في ذلك وعلم أنه لا يفعل مثل هذا، وكان يعينه وينصره، ولو استغاثه لدفع القوم بالحرب، وكان خرج إلى قرية يوم قتله وأقعد على باب الدار الحسن والحسين يحتطانه، فلما رجع عاتبهما فقالا: نقب عليه ولم نعلم، ولقد ترك محمد بن أبي بكر قصد قتله والإعانة عليه لما قال له: لو كان أبوك
And they ask him to allow them to fight them, but he used to refrain from that due to the meanings that have passed. That was when al-Hasan, al-Husayn, and Qanbar – may Allah be pleased with them – attended the house and repelled until they went out and were wounded, and it was not with him nor with any of the Companions – may Allah be pleased with them – that the matter would reach that extent, but the decree of Allah, the inevitable, was executed upon him, and he attained the martyrdom that was written for him. Checkpoint
What caused the uprising against Uthman according to the passage?
A) Uthman's personal misdeeds.
B) A forged letter by Marwan.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been wrongly accused of something you didn't do? How did you react? Would you be like Ali—who calmly affirmed the truth and continued to support the innocent—or would you abandon them? Ask Allah to grant you the courage to stand with the truth even when it's hard.
?
When you see injustice, are you quick to judge or do you investigate? The letter was forged, and the mob acted without verifying. Reflect on a time you acted on incomplete information. Repent and resolve to verify before acting.
?
Ali risked his sons to guard Uthman, and they failed to notice the assassin entering from behind. What 'backdoor' attacks might be threatening your faith or your family's faith? What steps can you take to guard against them starting today?

Defense of Ali from Uthman's Murder
Defends Ali against accusations of involvement in Uthman's murder.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how classical Sunni scholars defended Ali from allegations of involvement in Uthman's murder, using textual evidence and interpretation.

Core Idea
Ali was innocent of Uthman's blood, and his own words prove it.

This passage addresses a critical point of contention between Sunni and Shia Muslims: the role of Ali in Uthman's death. The author presents clear evidence from Ali's own statements and a prophetic dream to exonerate him, while also explaining how a controversial saying was misinterpreted.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic text
Read the passage from the beginning to 'والله الموفق' once to get the overall argument.
Focus on the rhetorical question and the quotes from Ali.
2
Identify the key claims
List the main assertions: Ali's denial, clarification of the ambiguous saying, and the prophecy of martyrdom.
Note how the author uses these to counter accusations.
3
Understand the author's strategy
Analyze how the author shifts from refutation to positive evidence, using a proverb and dream to reinforce Ali's innocence.
This shows the depth of the defense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يستعين بعلي ؟! وكيف يستنصر من هو جاد في نصره مشمر ذيله في ذلك؟! وروى عنه له أنه قال : - والله ما قتلت عثمان ولا مالات في قتله - وما روي عن علي ه أنه قال في أمر عثمان: الله قتله وأنا معه - معناه: وأنا مع عثمان وكانت الهاء عائدة إلى عثمان دون الله تعالى، وأخبر أنه يستشهد كما استشهد عثمان رضي الله عنهما. يحققه أنه قال على المنبر : - قتلت يوم قتل الثور الأبيض - وهو مثل مشهور في العرب، أخبر بذلك أنه يستشهد كما استشهد هو، والله الموفق. سبب مقتل عثمان : ثم سبب قتله معروف وهو أنه كان ولى بعض أقاربه مصر فجاء أهل مصر يشكونه إليه فعزله، وولى محمد بن أبي بكر وبعثه، ثم افتعل مروان كتابا كتبه بيده وختمه بخاتم عثمان لما أنه كان بيده من غير علم لعثمان وأرسله إليه على يد راكب جمل، وظُفر به وأنكر الكتاب وقال: فعله مروان، فقال له علي: لقد صدق، فصدقه علي في ذلك وعلم أنه لا يفعل مثل هذا، وكان يعينه وينصره، ولو استغاثه لدفع القوم بالحرب، وكان خرج إلى قرية يوم قتله وأقعد على باب الدار الحسن والحسين يحتطانه، فلما رجع عاتبهما فقالا: نُقبَ عليه ولم نعلم، ولقد ترك محمد بن أبي بكر قصد قتله والإعانة عليه لما قال له: لو كان أبوك في الأحياء لاستحييت منه - أو كما قال، فانصرف ثانيًا عنه، ثم أقدم عليه من لا له في فضل ولا يعد من العلماء ولا من الفضلاء، فقتله ظلما وهو يقرأ من سورة فسيكفيكهم الله وهو السميع العليم، وكان رأى النبي عليه السلام في منامه بارحة ذلك اليوم أنه قال: "لا تفطر حتى تفطر معي" فأصبح صائمًا منتظرا القضاء دافعا عن نفسه الردى بالتحصن بالدار متوكلاً على الله في أمره مفوضا أمره إليه متحرزاً عن إراقة دماء المسلمين حتى قال: لا أريد أن يراق في ولايتي قدر محجم من دم مسلم حين طلب منه الإذن فيه ليدفعوا الغوغاء والسفلة عنه.
He seeks help from Ali?! And how can he seek victory from one who is earnest in his support, rolling up his sleeves for that? And it is narrated from him that he said: 'By Allah, I did not kill Uthman nor did I assist in his killing.' And what is narrated from Ali that he said regarding the matter of Uthman: 'Allah killed him and I am with him' — its meaning: 'And I am with Uthman,' and the pronoun refers to Uthman, not to Allah. And he informed that he would be martyred just as Uthman was martyred, may Allah be pleased with them both. He confirmed it by saying on the pulpit: 'I was killed on the day the white bull was killed' — and it is a well-known proverb among the Arabs; he informed by that that he would be martyred just as he (Uthman) was martyred. And Allah is the Grantor of success. The reason for the killing of Uthman: Then the reason for his killing is known: that he appointed some of his relatives over Egypt, so the people of Egypt came complaining about them to him, so he removed him (the governor) and appointed Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr and sent him. Then Marwan forged a letter, wrote it with his own hand and sealed it with Uthman's ring, since it was in his possession, without Uthman's knowledge, and sent it to him (the previous governor) via a camel rider. It was intercepted, and he (Uthman) denied the letter and said: 'Marwan did it.' So Ali said to him: 'He has spoken the truth.' So Ali believed him in that and knew that he (Uthman) would not do such a thing. And he (Ali) was assisting and supporting him, and if he (Uthman) had sought his help, he would have repelled the people with war. And he (Uthman) had gone out to a village on the day of his killing and seated al-Hasan and al-Husayn at the door of the house protecting him. When he returned, he reproached them, and they said: 'A breach was made against him and we did not know.' And indeed Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr abandoned the intention of killing him and assisting in it when he said to him: 'If your father were alive, I would have been ashamed of him' — or as he said, so he turned away from him a second time. Then there advanced against him one who has no merit, nor is he counted among the scholars or the virtuous, so he killed him unjustly while he was reciting from the surah: 'So Allah will suffice you against them, and He is the All-Hearing, the All-Knowing.' And he (Uthman) had seen the Prophet, peace be upon him, in a dream the night before that day, saying: 'Do not break your fast until you break your fast with me.' So he started the day fasting, awaiting the decree, repelling destruction by fortifying himself in the house, relying on Allah in his affair, entrusting his affair to Him, cautious about shedding the blood of Muslims until he said: 'I do not want that a single drop of a Muslim's blood be shed in my governorate' — when permission was sought from him to repel the rabble and lowly people from him.
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage is a defense of Ali against allegations of involvement in Uthman's murder, followed by a detailed account of the events leading to Uthman's death. The author begins by refuting the notion that Ali would seek help from someone who was actively supporting him (Uthman) — i.e., Ali was a supporter, not an enemy. He then cites Ali's own words: 'By Allah, I did not kill Uthman nor did I assist in his killing.' The author clarifies a report where Ali said 'Allah killed him and I am with him,' explaining that 'with him' means with Uthman, not with Allah. Ali also predicted his own martyrdom, using a proverb. Next, the author narrates the cause: Uthman appointed relatives, causing complaints. He replaced the governor with Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr. Marwan forged a letter to the former governor ordering the killing of the new appointees. The letter was intercepted, and Uthman disowned it. Ali affirmed Uthman's truthfulness. Though Ali was ready to fight in Uthman's defense, Uthman wished to avoid bloodshed. He stationed al-Hasan and al-Husayn at his door. Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr abandoned his intent to kill Uthman after a remark about his father, Abu Bakr. Ultimately, base individuals killed Uthman while he was reciting Quran, fasting after a dream, and forbidding defensive violence to protect Muslim blood.

Key Terms
استشهاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ali was involved in or approved of Uthman's murder.
Correction: The passage shows Ali explicitly denied involvement and was a supporter of Uthman.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Ali mean when he said 'Allah killed him and I am with him'?
A) Ali approved of Uthman's killing as divine will.
B) 'Him' refers to Uthman, meaning Ali was with Uthman.
C) Allah and Ali jointly killed Uthman.
D) Ali was with Allah in decreeing Uthman's death.

Key Takeaway
Ali's own statements and a prophetic dream prove his innocence in Uthman's death.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever judged someone based on a misunderstanding of their words, as some judged Ali? What specific step from this lesson can you apply to prevent that in the future?
?
Ali predicted his own martyrdom and remained steadfast. If you were falsely accused and knew you would suffer, would you still defend the truth as Ali did? What holds you back?
?
When you hear a controversial statement about a fellow Muslim, do you rush to condemn or do you seek clarification like the author did? What would change if you adopted the author's method of verifying meanings before forming opinions?

The Story of Uthman's Murder
Narrates the events leading to Uthman's martyrdom and clears misconceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the chain of events that led to Uthman's martyrdom as narrated by the author, including the roles of Marwan, Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr, and Ali.

Core Idea
Uthman's murder was orchestrated by a forged letter and carried out by base individuals, despite his efforts to avoid bloodshed.

This passage narrates the tragic story of the third caliph's death, providing details about the political tensions, the forgery by Marwan, and the ultimate attack on Uthman's house. It highlights Ali's supportive role and Uthman's noble forbearance.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative
Read the passage from 'سبب مقتل عثمان' to the end to get the full story.
Pay attention to the sequence of events and key individuals.
2
Identify the key actors and their actions
List the main people: Uthman, Ali, Marwan, Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr, al-Hasan, al-Husayn, and the killers.
Note what each did and how they contributed to the outcome.
3
Understand Uthman's stance
Observe Uthman's desire to avoid bloodshed, his fasting after the dream, and his refusal to fight.
This shows his piety and forbearance.
4
Reflect on the moral
Consider the author's message: Uthman was innocent and killed unjustly by lowly people.
This reinforces the Sunni view of Uthman as a martyr.
